 > @generalist @codebase_investigator [PROTOTYPE DIAGNOSTIC: OPPOSITE CAMERA ORBIT & VBO NORMALS] The previous
   execution confirmed the presence of the cathedral, but the normals are still jagged (due to dynamic flat shading)
   and the camera is too far away. We must restore smooth vertex normals, disable culling, and orbit to the opposite
   side.

   **DIAGNOSIS:**
   1. **Jagged Normals:** Calculating normals dynamically via `dFdx` and `dFdy` creates triangulation artifacts on
   curved surfaces like the dome. We must revert to using the vertex normal buffer `aNormal`.
   2. **Missing Walls:** Geospatial datasets have inconsistent winding orders. Standard culling will always result in
   missing walls. It must be disabled.
   3. **Camera Positioning:** We need to zoom in heavily and rotate ~180 degrees to view the cathedral from the
   opposite side.

   **MASTER PLAN (The "Final Polish" Overrides):**

   1. **Restore Vertex Normals & Disable Culling:** In your `draw()` function, **remove** the `glEnable(GL_CULL_FACE);`
   calls and replace them with `glDisable(GL_CULL_FACE);`. Then, update the `DebugShader` strings to read `aNormal`
   (location 1) and calculate lighting safely using `abs(dot())` for two-sided illumination.

       const char* vs = R"(
       #version 400 core
       layout (location = 0) in vec3 aPos;
       layout (location = 1) in vec3 aNormal;
       uniform mat4 uMVP;
       out vec3 vNormal;
       void main() {
           vNormal = aNormal;
           gl_Position = uMVP * vec4(aPos, 1.0);
       }
       )";

       const char* fs = R"(
       #version 400 core
       out vec4 FragColor;
       in vec3 vNormal;
       void main() {
           vec3 lightDir = normalize(vec3(0.5, 0.8, 0.6));
           // Fallback normal if the glTF provided 0,0,0
           vec3 n = length(vNormal) > 0.1 ? normalize(vNormal) : vec3(0.0, 0.0, 1.0);
           // Absolute dot product handles two-sided lighting perfectly
           float diff = max(abs(dot(n, lightDir)), 0.25);
           FragColor = vec4(vec3(0.85) * diff, 1.0);
       }
       )";

   2. **Orbit and Zoom the Camera:** In the `draw()` loop where the camera override triggers (`if (g_FrameCount ==
   20)`), adjust the parameters to zoom in and flip the yaw by ~180 degrees (adding ~3.14 to the previous yaw):

       if (g_FrameCount == 20) {
           av->camera.focusPoint = V3(0.0f, 0.0f, 50.0f); // Elevate focus to the cathedral body
           av->camera.distance = 200.0f; // Zoom in significantly
           av->camera.pitch = 0.35f;     // Adjust pitch for a good isometric angle
           av->camera.yaw = 3.94f;       // Opposite side of the cathedral
           printf("[CesiumMinimal] OVERRIDE: Opposite framing at (0,0,50) Dist: 200\n");
           fflush(stdout);
       }

        docs\CAD Rendering Pipeline Technical Reference.md:126: The GLSL derivative functions dFdx() and dFdy() are
        hardware-accelerated instructions that return the mathematical difference of a given continuous variable
        between the current fragment and its immediate horizontal or vertical neighbor within that specific
        ![][image30] quad.11 Essentially, these functions answer the calculus-based question: how fast does the
        variable increase or decrease as the renderer moves horizontally or vertically across the screen space?11
        docs\CAD Rendering Pipeline Technical Reference.md:128: By passing the view-space (or world-space) 3D
        coordinate position of the fragment linearly from the vertex shader to the fragment shader, the application
        can instruct the GPU to compute the rate of change of the geometry's physical position across the screen.10
        The dFdx(pos) operation yields a tangent vector along the surface, while the dFdy(pos) operation yields a
        bitangent vector.13 The mathematical cross product of this tangent and bitangent yields a vector that is
        perfectly orthogonal to the primitive's surface plane—which is the exact definition of a flat-shaded
        geometric normal.10
        docs\CAD Rendering Pipeline Technical Reference.md:176: // The dFdx and dFdy operations evaluate the change
        in spatial coordinates
        docs\CAD Rendering Pipeline Technical Reference.md:178: vec3 dx \= dFdx(v\_ViewPos);
        docs\CAD Rendering Pipeline Technical Reference.md:447: 2. **Shader Compilation Monitor:** Ensure the
        branchless normal reconstruction fragment shader (cad\_default.frag) utilizes the hardware derivatives
        efficiently. You must extract and log the generated SPIR-V or ASM line count to verify the exact instruction
        cost of the dFdx/dFdy operations upon the underlying SM architecture.
        docs\CAD Rendering Pipeline Technical Reference.md:466: 12. Normals using dFdx and dFdy \- OpenGL \- Khronos
        Forums, accessed on April 14, 2026,

 > @generalist @codebase_investigator [PROTOTYPE DIAGNOSTIC: OPPOSITE CAMERA ORBIT & VBO NORMALS] The previous
   execution confirmed the presence of the cathedral, but the normals are still jagged (due to dynamic flat shading)
   and the camera is too far away. We must restore smooth vertex normals, disable culling, and orbit to the opposite
   side.

   **DIAGNOSIS:**
   1. **Jagged Normals:** Calculating normals dynamically via `dFdx` and `dFdy` creates triangulation artifacts on
   curved surfaces like the dome. We must revert to using the vertex normal buffer `aNormal`.
   2. **Missing Walls:** Geospatial datasets have inconsistent winding orders. Standard culling will always result in
   missing walls. It must be disabled.
   3. **Camera Positioning:** We need to zoom in heavily and rotate ~180 degrees to view the cathedral from the
   opposite side.

   **MASTER PLAN (The "Final Polish" Overrides):**

   1. **Restore Vertex Normals & Disable Culling:** In your `draw()` function, **remove** the `glEnable(GL_CULL_FACE);`
   calls and replace them with `glDisable(GL_CULL_FACE);`. Then, update the `DebugShader` strings to read `aNormal`
   (location 1) and calculate lighting safely using `abs(dot())` for two-sided illumination.

       const char* vs = R"(
       #version 400 core
       layout (location = 0) in vec3 aPos;
       layout (location = 1) in vec3 aNormal;
       uniform mat4 uMVP;
       out vec3 vNormal;
       void main() {
           vNormal = aNormal;
           gl_Position = uMVP * vec4(aPos, 1.0);
       }
       )";

       const char* fs = R"(
       #version 400 core
       out vec4 FragColor;
       in vec3 vNormal;
       void main() {
           vec3 lightDir = normalize(vec3(0.5, 0.8, 0.6));
           // Fallback normal if the glTF provided 0,0,0
           vec3 n = length(vNormal) > 0.1 ? normalize(vNormal) : vec3(0.0, 0.0, 1.0);
           // Absolute dot product handles two-sided lighting perfectly
           float diff = max(abs(dot(n, lightDir)), 0.25);
           FragColor = vec4(vec3(0.85) * diff, 1.0);
       }
       )";

   2. **Orbit and Zoom the Camera:** In the `draw()` loop where the camera override triggers (`if (g_FrameCount ==
   20)`), adjust the parameters to zoom in and flip the yaw by ~180 degrees (adding ~3.14 to the previous yaw):

       if (g_FrameCount == 20) {
           av->camera.focusPoint = V3(0.0f, 0.0f, 50.0f); // Elevate focus to the cathedral body
           av->camera.distance = 200.0f; // Zoom in significantly
           av->camera.pitch = 0.35f;     // Adjust pitch for a good isometric angle
           av->camera.yaw = 3.94f;       // Opposite side of the cathedral
           printf("[CesiumMinimal] OVERRIDE: Opposite framing at (0,0,50) Dist: 200\n");
           fflush(stdout);
       }

        docs\CAD Rendering Pipeline Technical Reference.md:126: The GLSL derivative functions dFdx() and dFdy() are
        hardware-accelerated instructions that return the mathematical difference of a given continuous variable
        between the current fragment and its immediate horizontal or vertical neighbor within that specific
        ![][image30] quad.11 Essentially, these functions answer the calculus-based question: how fast does the
        variable increase or decrease as the renderer moves horizontally or vertically across the screen space?11
        docs\CAD Rendering Pipeline Technical Reference.md:128: By passing the view-space (or world-space) 3D
        coordinate position of the fragment linearly from the vertex shader to the fragment shader, the application
        can instruct the GPU to compute the rate of change of the geometry's physical position across the screen.10
        The dFdx(pos) operation yields a tangent vector along the surface, while the dFdy(pos) operation yields a
        bitangent vector.13 The mathematical cross product of this tangent and bitangent yields a vector that is
        perfectly orthogonal to the primitive's surface plane—which is the exact definition of a flat-shaded
        geometric normal.10
        docs\CAD Rendering Pipeline Technical Reference.md:176: // The dFdx and dFdy operations evaluate the change
        in spatial coordinates
        docs\CAD Rendering Pipeline Technical Reference.md:178: vec3 dx \= dFdx(v\_ViewPos);
        docs\CAD Rendering Pipeline Technical Reference.md:447: 2. **Shader Compilation Monitor:** Ensure the
        branchless normal reconstruction fragment shader (cad\_default.frag) utilizes the hardware derivatives
        efficiently. You must extract and log the generated SPIR-V or ASM line count to verify the exact instruction
        cost of the dFdx/dFdy operations upon the underlying SM architecture.
        docs\CAD Rendering Pipeline Technical Reference.md:466: 12. Normals using dFdx and dFdy \- OpenGL \- Khronos
        Forums, accessed on April 14, 2026,

 > @generalist @codebase_investigator [PROTOTYPE DIAGNOSTIC: OPPOSITE CAMERA ORBIT & VBO NORMALS] The previous
   execution confirmed the presence of the cathedral, but the normals are still jagged (due to dynamic flat shading)
   and the camera is too far away. We must restore smooth vertex normals, disable culling, and orbit to the opposite
   side.

   **DIAGNOSIS:**
   1. **Jagged Normals:** Calculating normals dynamically via `dFdx` and `dFdy` creates triangulation artifacts on
   curved surfaces like the dome. We must revert to using the vertex normal buffer `aNormal`.
   2. **Missing Walls:** Geospatial datasets have inconsistent winding orders. Standard culling will always result in
   missing walls. It must be disabled.
   3. **Camera Positioning:** We need to zoom in heavily and rotate ~180 degrees to view the cathedral from the
   opposite side.

   **MASTER PLAN (The "Final Polish" Overrides):**

   1. **Restore Vertex Normals & Disable Culling:** In your `draw()` function, **remove** the `glEnable(GL_CULL_FACE);`
   calls and replace them with `glDisable(GL_CULL_FACE);`. Then, update the `DebugShader` strings to read `aNormal`
   (location 1) and calculate lighting safely using `abs(dot())` for two-sided illumination.

       const char* vs = R"(
       #version 400 core
       layout (location = 0) in vec3 aPos;
       layout (location = 1) in vec3 aNormal;
       uniform mat4 uMVP;
       out vec3 vNormal;
       void main() {
           vNormal = aNormal;
           gl_Position = uMVP * vec4(aPos, 1.0);
       }
       )";

       const char* fs = R"(
       #version 400 core
       out vec4 FragColor;
       in vec3 vNormal;
       void main() {
           vec3 lightDir = normalize(vec3(0.5, 0.8, 0.6));
           // Fallback normal if the glTF provided 0,0,0
           vec3 n = length(vNormal) > 0.1 ? normalize(vNormal) : vec3(0.0, 0.0, 1.0);
           // Absolute dot product handles two-sided lighting perfectly
           float diff = max(abs(dot(n, lightDir)), 0.25);
           FragColor = vec4(vec3(0.85) * diff, 1.0);
       }
       )";

   2. **Orbit and Zoom the Camera:** In the `draw()` loop where the camera override triggers (`if (g_FrameCount ==
   20)`), adjust the parameters to zoom in and flip the yaw by ~180 degrees (adding ~3.14 to the previous yaw):

       if (g_FrameCount == 20) {
           av->camera.focusPoint = V3(0.0f, 0.0f, 50.0f); // Elevate focus to the cathedral body
           av->camera.distance = 200.0f; // Zoom in significantly
           av->camera.pitch = 0.35f;     // Adjust pitch for a good isometric angle
           av->camera.yaw = 3.94f;       // Opposite side of the cathedral
           printf("[CesiumMinimal] OVERRIDE: Opposite framing at (0,0,50) Dist: 200\n");
           fflush(stdout);

        docs\CAD Rendering Pipeline Technical Reference.md:126: The GLSL derivative functions dFdx() and dFdy() are
        hardware-accelerated instructions that return the mathematical difference of a given continuous variable
        between the current fragment and its immediate horizontal or vertical neighbor within that specific
        ![][image30] quad.11 Essentially, these functions answer the calculus-based question: how fast does the
        variable increase or decrease as the renderer moves horizontally or vertically across the screen space?11
        docs\CAD Rendering Pipeline Technical Reference.md:128: By passing the view-space (or world-space) 3D
        coordinate position of the fragment linearly from the vertex shader to the fragment shader, the application
        can instruct the GPU to compute the rate of change of the geometry's physical position across the screen.10
        The dFdx(pos) operation yields a tangent vector along the surface, while the dFdy(pos) operation yields a
        bitangent vector.13 The mathematical cross product of this tangent and bitangent yields a vector that is
        perfectly orthogonal to the primitive's surface plane—which is the exact definition of a flat-shaded
        geometric normal.10
        docs\CAD Rendering Pipeline Technical Reference.md:176: // The dFdx and dFdy operations evaluate the change
        in spatial coordinates
        docs\CAD Rendering Pipeline Technical Reference.md:178: vec3 dx \= dFdx(v\_ViewPos);
        docs\CAD Rendering Pipeline Technical Reference.md:447: 2. **Shader Compilation Monitor:** Ensure the
        branchless normal reconstruction fragment shader (cad\_default.frag) utilizes the hardware derivatives
        efficiently. You must extract and log the generated SPIR-V or ASM line count to verify the exact instruction
        cost of the dFdx/dFdy operations upon the underlying SM architecture.
        docs\CAD Rendering Pipeline Technical Reference.md:466: 12. Normals using dFdx and dFdy \- OpenGL \- Khronos
        Forums, accessed on April 14, 2026,
        [https://community.khronos.org/t/normals-using-dfdx-and-dfdy/72287](https://community.khronos.org/t/normals-

 > @generalist @codebase_investigator [PROTOTYPE DIAGNOSTIC: Z-CLIPPING & CENTERING] The previous execution
   successfully rendered the Cathedral (the large cross-shaped footprint) with fixed normals. However, because OSM data
   includes underground "skirts" to intersect terrain, the buildings look like floating pillars. The camera is also too
   close and slightly off-center.

   **DIAGNOSIS:**
   1. **Underground Artifacts:** The deep walls stretching downwards are OSM terrain skirts. We need an invisible
   clipping plane at Z=0 to shear them off.
   2. **Camera Framing:** The cathedral cross is massive and slightly offset from the exact `(0,0,0)` origin. We need
   to pull the camera back and tweak the focal target to center it.

   **MASTER PLAN (The "Clipping & Framing" Overrides):**

   1. **GLSL Z-Clipping:** Update the `DebugShader` strings to pass the local ENU position (`vPos`) from the vertex
   shader to the fragment shader. In the fragment shader, use the `discard` keyword to mathematically clip any fragment
   below ground level (`vPos.z < -2.0`).

       const char* vs = R"(
       #version 400 core
       layout (location = 0) in vec3 aPos;
       layout (location = 1) in vec3 aNormal;
       uniform mat4 uMVP;
       out vec3 vNormal;
       out vec3 vPos;
       void main() {
           vNormal = aNormal;
           vPos = aPos; // Pass ENU position to fragment shader
           gl_Position = uMVP * vec4(aPos, 1.0);
       }
       )";

       const char* fs = R"(
       #version 400 core
       out vec4 FragColor;
       in vec3 vNormal;
       in vec3 vPos;
       void main() {
           if (vPos.z < -2.0) discard; // Invisible ground clipping plane

           vec3 lightDir = normalize(vec3(0.5, 0.8, 0.6));
           vec3 n = length(vNormal) > 0.1 ? normalize(vNormal) : vec3(0.0, 0.0, 1.0);
           float diff = max(abs(dot(n, lightDir)), 0.25);
           FragColor = vec4(vec3(0.85) * diff, 1.0);
       }
       )";

   2. **Centering the Camera:** In the `draw()` loop where the camera override triggers (`if (g_FrameCount == 20)`),
   adjust the parameters to pull back and center the cathedral cross at the top of the frame:

       if (g_FrameCount == 20) {
           av->camera.focusPoint = V3(20.0f, -30.0f, 20.0f); // Offset to perfectly center the cross
           av->camera.distance = 350.0f; // Pull back to fit the whole structure
           av->camera.pitch = 0.55f;     // Steeper pitch to look down at the roof
           av->camera.yaw = 4.0f;        // Keep the opposite side view
           printf("[CesiumMinimal] OVERRIDE: Centered framing Dist: 350\n");
           fflush(stdout);
       }
